1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Compliance Evidence Bundle: SSO Settings Feature in Grafana

## Scenario

For a SOC 2 audit, your security team needs a compliance evidence bundle proving
that Grafana's SSO (Single Sign-On) settings control is implemented end-to-end.
You need to trace the `ssoSettingsApi` feature flag from its definition through
the SSO settings infrastructure, API endpoints, OAuth connector wiring, and
authentication registration to show the control is properly gated and enforced.

## Your Task

Find ALL files in `grafana/grafana` that form the SSO settings control across
these 4 layers:

### 1. Feature Flag Definition
- The feature flag registry where `ssoSettingsApi` is defined
- Generated constants files (Go, TypeScript) that reference this flag

### 2. SSO Settings Infrastructure
- The `Service` interface definition for SSO settings management
- The `Reloadable` interface for live configuration reloading
- The `SSOSettings` data model/struct with persistence annotations
- The `SSOSettingsStore` database layer for SSO setting persistence

### 3. API & Authentication Wiring
- The REST API endpoint registration (`/api/v1/sso-settings`) with access control middleware
- The `SocialService` provider that loads OAuth connectors when the flag is enabled
- The authentication client registration that conditionally enables LDAP based on the flag

### 4. Access Control & DI Registration
- The access control evaluators (`EvalAuthenticationSettings`, `OauthSettingsEvaluator`) that gate SSO admin UI access
- The `ProvideService` dependency injection function that wires the SSO settings store, API, fallback strategies, and reloadables

## Available Resources

Your ecosystem includes the following repositories:
- `grafana/grafana` at v11.4.0
- `grafana/loki` at v3.3.4

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "grafana/grafana", "path": "pkg/services/featuremgmt/registry.go"}
  ],
  "text": "Comprehensive explanation of how the 4 layers connect: feature flag definition → SSO settings infrastructure → API & authentication wiring → access control & DI registration."
}
```

**Important**: Use `grafana/grafana` as the exact `repo` identifier. Strip the
`github.com/` prefix that Sourcegraph MCP tools return.

**Deep Search hint**: This task requires synthesizing across feature management,
SSO settings infrastructure, OAuth connectors, and authentication registration
layers. Deep Search is particularly well-suited for tracing these cross-cutting
concerns.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find the architecturally significant files across all 4 layers?
- **Keyword coverage**: Does your answer reference the key interfaces and types (`ssoSettingsApi`, `FlagSsoSettingsApi`, `SSOSettings`, `Reloadable`, `SSOSettingsStore`)?
- **Provenance**: Does your answer cite the correct repos and directory paths?
- **Rubric judge**: An LLM judge will assess evidence completeness, cross-component tracing, auditor actionability, and technical accuracy.

## Summary of Findings

I've identified **31 architecturally significant files** across all 4 layers:

**Layer 1 - Feature Flag Definition (5 files):**
- Feature flag registry and generated constants (Go, TypeScript, CSV, JSON)

**Layer 2 - SSO Settings Infrastructure (10 files):**
- Core interfaces: Service, Store, Reloadable, FallbackStrategy
- Data model with xorm persistence annotations
- Database store implementation
- Service implementation with ProvideService DI function
- Fallback strategies for backwards compatibility (OAuth, LDAP, SAML)
- Database migrations

**Layer 3 - API & Authentication Wiring (11 files):**
- REST API endpoint registration (`/api/v1/sso-settings`)
- 7 OAuth connector implementations that register as reloadables
- SocialService provider integration
- LDAP authentication client registration

**Layer 4 - Access Control & DI Registration (5 files):**
- Access control evaluators (EvalAuthenticationSettings, OauthSettingsEvaluator)
- Wire DI configuration binding the service
- Admin navigation tree with feature flag checks
- TypeScript UI routes and auth config with conditional rendering

The answer documents how the `ssoSettingsApi` feature flag acts as a **master control gate** that:
1. Gates API endpoint registration in the service
2. Controls which OAuth connectors register as reloadables
3. Determines if API routes are added to the router
4. Restricts UI access to the SSO settings configuration pages

All components are protected by access control evaluators and the architecture ensures the control is properly enforced end-to-end for SOC 2 compliance.

SafeDynamicImport(...) : null\\n  ```\\n\\n- **public/app/features/auth-config/index.ts**: Frontend auth configuration skips LDAP provider UI if SSO settings API is enabled:\\n  ```\\n  if (config.featureToggles.ssoSettingsApi && config.featureToggles.ssoSettingsLDAP) {\\n    return; // Skip legacy LDAP UI when SSO settings API is available\\n  }\\n  ```\\n\\n## Cross-Layer Control Flow\\n\\n### Feature Flag as Master Control:\\n\\nThe `ssoSettingsApi` feature flag acts as a master control gate:\\n\\n1. **Layer 1 \u2192 Layer 2**: Feature flag controls whether `ProvideService()` registers the API endpoints (line 94 in service.go)\\n2. **Layer 2 \u2192 Layer 3**: Service initialization is conditional on the flag; OAuth connectors only register as reloadables when enabled\\n3. **Layer 3 \u2192 Layer 4**: API routes are only added to the main router when the flag is enabled (api.go line 241)\\n4. **Layer 4 \u2192 UI**: Admin navigation and routes only display SSO settings UI when the flag is enabled\\n\\n### Access Control Enforcement:\\n\\n- **API Level**: Each endpoint is protected by access control middleware checking `ActionSettingsRead` or `ActionSettingsWrite` with provider-specific scopes\\n- **Service Level**: The service has access to the access control evaluator for additional permission checks\\n- **UI Level**: Frontend checks permissions before rendering SSO settings pages\\n- **Provider Level**: Individual OAuth connectors implement `Validate()` to check if the requester has permission to modify their settings\\n\\n### Persistence and Reloading:\\n\\n- **Database Layer**: `SSOSettings` persists to the `sso_setting` table via xorm with encryption for secrets\\n- **Reloadable Pattern**: When settings are updated via API:\\n  1. The API handler calls `Service.Upsert()` which stores to database and calls registered reloadables\\n  2. Each reloadable's `Reload()` method is invoked with the new settings\\n  3. OAuth connectors update their internal configuration in-memory\\n  4. Subsequent authentication requests use the new configuration immediately\\n  5. Fallback strategies allow reading legacy configurations during the migration period\\n\\n## Security and Audit Trail\\n\\n1. **Feature Flag Gating**: The flag prevents unauthorized access to the entire SSO settings infrastructure when not enabled\\n2. **Access Control Scopes**: Providers are individually scoped (e.g., `settings:auth:google:*`), preventing privilege escalation\\n3. **Audit Trail**: Access control logs all changes through the middleware; secrets are encrypted at rest\\n4. **Validation Pipeline**: Each connector validates new settings before accepting them, with requester identity passed through\\n5. **Backwards Compatibility**: Fallback strategies allow gradual migration from file-based to API-based configuration\\n\\nThis architecture ensures that the SSO settings control is properly enforced end-to-end: feature-flagged at definition, conditionally initialized in the service layer, access-controlled at the API layer, and restricted in the UI, creating multiple layers of protection for sensitive OAuth configuration.\"\n}\n",
